<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150922"><span lang="EN-GB">openHAB2 configuration for the
samba server:</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">This is required to grant the PC based
Eclipse Smart Home Designer access to the requested configuration folder on
your Raspbian. </span></p>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">The shares are configured to be not open for guests
  nor to the public. Let’s activate the “openhab” user as a samba user</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: solid solid solid none; border-color: windowtext windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: 1pt 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">sudo smbpasswd -a openhab</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Enter the password </span><i>openhabpassword</i></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">New SMB password:</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Retype new SMB password:</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">Added user openhab.</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Be aware, that creating and later using a specific
  user will ensure that permissions are honoured. Make sure, the “openhab” user
  has ownership and/or write access to the openHAB2 configuration files. This
  can be accomplished by executing:</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">sudo chown -hR openhab:openhab /etc/openhab2</span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Restart the samba service to allow the changes to be
  utilized</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">sudo systemctl restart smbd.service</span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">One time map the Raspberry folder to a windows drive
  (in this case </span><span lang="EN-US">Z</span><span lang="EN-GB">) enter in the
  CMD Prompt (just put </span><span lang="EN-US">CMD</span><span lang="EN-GB"> in
  the search of Windows 10 to open the command prompt)</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">net use Z: \\<i>xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx</i>\RaspberryPiDirectories
  /user:openhab <i>openhabpassword </i>/persistent:no</span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Optional: Persistent map the Raspberry folder to a
  windows drive (in this case </span><span lang="EN-US">Z</span><span lang="EN-GB">)
  enter in the CMD Prompt (just put </span><span lang="EN-US">CMD</span><span lang="EN-GB"> in the search of Windows 10 to open the command prompt)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE: Now every time you boot up your PC it will try
  to connect to the Raspbian samba server.</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: Consolas; color: rgb(112, 173, 71);" lang="EN-GB">net use
  Z: \\xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx\RaspberryPiDirectories /user:openhab openhabpassword
  /persistent:yes</span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.95pt;" valign="top" width="320">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Optional: You can also create a simple *.bat file
  for easy double clicking.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Open the editor by just putting </span><span lang="EN-US">notepad</span><span lang="EN-GB"> in the search of Windows 10</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Enter the line</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Save as </span><i><span lang="EN-US">yourmapping</span></i><span lang="EN-US">.bat</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 252.75pt;" valign="top" width="337">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-family: Consolas; color: rgb(112, 173, 71);" lang="EN-GB">net use
  Z: \\xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx\RaspberryPiDirectories /user:openhab openhabpassword
  /persistent:no </span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</tbody></table>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-GB"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150923"><span lang="EN-GB">openHAB2 Privileges for Common Peripherals</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">An openHAB2 setup will often rely on
hardware like a modem, transceiver or adapter to interface with home automation
hardware. Examples are a Z-Wave, Enocean or RXFcom USB Stick or a Raspberry Pi
add-on board connected to the serial port on its GPIOs. In order to allow
openHAB2 to communicate with additional peripherals, it has to be added to
corresponding Linux groups. The following example shows how to add Linux user openHAB2
to the often needed groups </span><span lang="EN-US">dialout</span><span lang="EN-GB"> and </span><span lang="EN-US">tty</span><span lang="EN-GB">. Additional
groups may be needed, depending on your hardware and software setup.</span></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc485150924"><span lang="EN-GB">Adding openhab user to groupds
dialout an tty</span></a></h3>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Open Terminal</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: solid solid solid none; border-color: windowtext windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: 1pt 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 128" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image076.jpg" alt="Ähnliches Foto" border="0" height="26" width="31"><img id="Picture 129" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image080.jpg" border="0" height="24" width="167"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Enter command</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">(This is adding the </span><span lang="EN-US">openhab</span><span lang="EN-GB"> user to the group </span><span lang="EN-US">dialout</span><span lang="EN-GB">)</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">sudo adduser openhab dialout</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Enter command</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">(This is adding the </span><span lang="EN-US">openhab</span><span lang="EN-GB"> user to the group </span><span lang="EN-US">tty</span><span lang="EN-GB">)</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">sudo adduser openhab tty</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Optional: Enter command</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">(f you are looking to enable sound privileges for
  openHAB2, it will also be necessary to add openHAB2 to the “audio” group.)</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">sudo adduser openhab audio</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</tbody></table>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Change the text from (nothing between the “”)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">To (something between the “”)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 240.95pt;" valign="top" width="321">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">EXTRA_JAVA_OPTS=""</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">EXTRA_JAVA_OPTS="-Dgnu.io.rxtx.SerialPorts=/dev/ttyUSB0:/dev/ttyS0:/dev/ttyS2:/dev/ttyACM0:/dev/ttyAMA0"</span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 246.4pt;" valign="top" width="329">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Exit and save the file </span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 240.95pt;" valign="top" width="321">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;ctrl+x&gt;</p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;y&gt;</p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;Enter&gt;</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 246.4pt;" valign="top" width="329">

  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 240.95pt;" valign="top" width="321">

  </td>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150926"><span lang="EN-GB">Chapter 7: Installation of Eclipse
Smart Home Designer</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">(Optional but strongly recommended for easy
editing of openHAB2 configuration files; incl. syntax highlighting)</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">The complete installation guide can be
found on : </span><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/installation/designer.html#setup"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">http://docs.openhab.org/installation/designer.html#setup</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Download the 64bit version (something like
  jre-8u131-windows-x64.exe ) or the 32bit depending on your system</span></p>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Install the Java Runtime Environment to the Eclipse
  Smart Home Designer folder</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Start the Java installer</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Select on the first screen “Change destination
  folder”</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Change the folder to \jre inside your Eclipse Smart
  Home Designer folder </span><i><span lang="EN-US">yourpcdrive:\yourdestionation\eclipseSmart
  Home</span></i><span lang="EN-GB">since this is the loaction your Eclipse Smart
  Home Designer is expecting the JRE.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE: This is now delivering you a “portable”
  version of the Eclipse Smart Home Designer which just can be copied/moved to
  different locations or machines without the need of reinstalling.</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 274.65pt;" valign="top" width="366">

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&lt;Change&gt;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><i><span lang="EN-US">yourpcdrive:\yourdestionation\</span></i><span lang="EN-US">eclipsesmarthome\jre</span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150929"><span lang="EN-GB">Chapter 8: Initializing openHAB2 (finally:
first startup)</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">To open the openHAB2 you have to access the
web GUI with a browser on your PC or directly from your Raspberry, depending on
your setup.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">The URL will be </span><span lang="EN-US">http://<i>xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx</i>:8080/start/index
</span><span lang="EN-GB">filling in the IP of your Raspberry</span></p>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 210.4pt;" valign="top" width="281">

  setup configuration.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">This will install a standard set of GUIs in openHAB2</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: solid solid solid none; border-color: windowtext windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: 1pt 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 282.3pt;" valign="top" width="376">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 93" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image109.jpg" border="0" height="270" width="362"></p>

your home automation project in openHAB2!</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-GB"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150930"><span lang="EN-GB">Chapter 10: General information
about configuring openHAB2</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">Make sure to double check with the official
website of openHAB2 since in the end this is where you will find the correct
answers if something in this tutorial is not working:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://www.openhab.org/"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">http://www.openhab.org/</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">As a start you should read the beginners
tutorial form beginning to end so you understand the basic concept of things,
items, rules etc. and how they are mend to work together;</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/introduction.html"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">http://docs.openhab.org/introduction.html</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150931"><span lang="EN-GB">openHAB (no 2) vs. openHAB2</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">One of the most important things I had to
learn is that there is also an openHAB (no 2)! So here are a few things if
found out to be considerable if you are using openHAB2:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 36pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">-<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">Always make sure, that you are looking at the
right version of openHAB when it comes down to documentation, since a lot of
older online documentation is refereeing to the openHAB (no 2). When a few
things might be done the same/similar way in openHAB2, other things have
changed and will not work in openHAB2</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 36pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">-<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">You will also encounter two different ways of
storing configuration in openHAB.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 72pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Courier New&quot;;" lang="EN-GB">o<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">In openHAB (no 2).configuration was stored in
files only</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 72pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Courier New&quot;;" lang="EN-GB">o<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">In openHAB2 you can still use the files, but
also can use database storage for certain typs when you do the configuration
with PAPER UI. This now might lead to some confusion since you will not be able
to change e.g. items in PAPER UI which were configured using a text file. Also
you would not have the correct syntax highlighting in the Eclipse Smart Home
Designer is expecting file configuration only an items configured in PAPER UI
will show up as errors.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 72pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Courier New&quot;;" lang="EN-GB">o<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">But be aware that some configuration in openHAB2
still has to be done via text file like e.g. rules. You might find already some
progress in the snapshot release of openHAB2, but I decided to base this
tutorial on the stable release with limited functionality in PAPER UI database</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 36pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">-<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">Regularly check the website of openHAB2 for news
since a lot of new features are expected to be implemented.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 36pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">-<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">Meanwhile be not afraid to go and sign up the
openHAB community:</span><span lang="EN-GB"> </span><a href="https://community.openhab.org"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">h</span></span><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">ttps://community.openhab.org</span></span></a><span lang="EN-GB"> and ask your questions there. I got replies to my problems within
days, sometimes even within hrs. There is also a designated area for beginners.</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-GB"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150932"><span lang="EN-GB">Chapter 10: Configuring openHAB2
using PAPER UI</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">Since the online documentation is mostly
referring to PAPER UI GUI I will try to stick to this GUI as long as possible. </span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 36pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">-<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">HABmin GUI will be needed for some&nbsp; Z-Wave
installation</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 36pt; text-indent: -18pt;"><span lang="EN-GB">-<span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-size-adjust: none; font-stretch: normal;">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span></span><span lang="EN-GB">HABPANEL GUI will be used to create the final
user frontend for this project</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE: Since you will be regularly starting
and switching the GUIs I highly recommend creating quick links in your browser
for each GUI</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150934"><span lang="EN-GB">General process of adding new
things to the configuration</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE: If you can add new things to openHAB2
depends on whether they are connected to the network (if you use IP), whether
they are included in the Z-Wave network of the Z-Wave controller or whether
your Raspberry is online if you use online sourced like YahooWeather</span></p>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

  already connected to the same network than my Raspberry, I do already get a
  message in the inbox which is telling me, that a new thing was found</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Now just click on the blue icon with the check mark
  to add this thing</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: solid solid solid none; border-color: windowtext windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: 1pt 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

<p class="MsoNormal"><b><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE:</span></b><span lang="EN-GB"> Make
sure that the device is connected to the Raspberry network via IP.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150939"><span lang="EN-GB">Adding online things connected via
network (IP)</span></a></h2>

sure the Raspbian does have online access pages.</span></p>

Binding:</span></a></h3>

  (+) </span></p>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

  Information&gt;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Now you have to configure the thing</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">In this case you have to enter the WOEID which is a
  32-bit reference identifier of the location you want to see the weather
  information for.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">You can look up the WOEID on e.g.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><a href="http://www.woeidlookup.com/"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">http://www.woeidlookup.com/</span></span></a></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">In this case we choose Berlin </span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">WOEID: </span><span lang="EN-US">638242</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">More information on WOEID on:</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WOEID"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WOEID</span></span></a></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 146" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image134.jpg" border="0" height="198" width="285"></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150941"><span lang="EN-GB">Adding things connected via Z-Wave
controller</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><b><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE:</span></b><span lang="EN-GB"> first
you have to connect the Z-Wave controller as a thing. After this you will use
HABmin to further include things into the Z-Wave network. These things should
show up automatically in the inbox of PAPER UI.</span></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc485150942"><span lang="EN-GB">Adding Z-Wave controller</span></a></h3>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Select in your PAPER UI inbox the add blue add icon
  (+) </span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: solid solid solid none; border-color: windowtext windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: 1pt 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 169" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image122.jpg" border="0" height="82" width="188"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Select the Binding </span><span lang="EN-US">&lt;Z-Wave
  Binding&gt;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 175" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image136.jpg" border="0" height="98" width="302"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Select the thing </span><span lang="EN-US">&lt;Z-Wave
  Serial Controller&gt;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 176" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image137.jpg" border="0" height="47" width="304"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Now you have to configure the thing</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">In this case you have to enter the serial Port of
  the Z-Wave controller</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">The standard port where the UBS-Z-Wave controller
  should come up it:</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">/dev/ttyACM0</p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 177" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image138.jpg" border="0" height="181" width="261"></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">/dev/ttyACM0</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Then just add the thing by clicking on the blue
  check icon</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 178" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image139.jpg" border="0" height="184" width="266"></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;(+)&gt;</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">The green icon online next to the name is indicating
  that openHAB2 is connected to the thing and information can be exchanged</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

  </td>

</tbody></table>

<h3><a name="_Toc485150943"><span lang="EN-GB">Adding Z-Wave things using HABmin
UI</span></a></h3>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">To include further devices into your Z-Wave
network and make the available as openHAB2 things you have to use the HABmin
inclusion functionality.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">Please also consult the online
documentation for general information about Z-Wave : </span><a href="https://github.com/openhab/org.openhab.ui.habmin/wiki/ZWave-Device-Installation"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">https://github.com/openhab/org.openhab.ui.habmin/wiki/ZWave-Device-Installation</span></span></a></p>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">And when a device is found it will be listed </span></p>

  device as a thing for openHAB2</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">NOTE: some devices may come up as <b>“unknown
  device”</b>. You can still add the device and “cure” the information later.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">The normal reason for this is that the device was
  not able to finish the communication with HABmin during the inclusion process</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">This might be very likely for battery powered
  devices since the will go to sleep mode after a certain amount of time. To
  cure this you just have to manually wake up the device (see device manual)
  multiple times (up to 10 times) before the communication is completed and the
  device is recognized as a proper thing in HABmin</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">ATTENTION: Using the <b>Aeotec by Aeon Labs Z-Stick
  Gen5</b> almost every battery powered item will come up as <b>“unknown
  device” </b>since in the timespan you include the battery device to the stick
  and you do the HABmin inclusion after you plugged the stick back in will be
  to long an most of the devices will go back to sleep. You might prevent this
  by manually waking up the device again just seconds before you start the
  inclusion on HABmin.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">The other reason is that the device is not supported
  by the openHAB2 Z-Wave binding. You can check the supported devices at:</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">http://www.cd-jackson.com/index.php/zwave/zwave-device-database/zwave-device-list</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 246.3pt;" valign="top" width="328">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 194" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image146.png" alt="http://www.cd-jackson.com/images/habmin/HABmin-Things-discovery_inbox.png" border="0" height="164" width="247"></p>
  </td>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">The newly added thing should now be visible in the

<h3><a name="_Toc485150944"><span lang="EN-GB">For details documentation on the
Z-Wave Binding usage in HABmin consult:</span></a></h3>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://www.cd-jackson.com/index.php/openhab/habmin/10-habmin-zwave-binding-initialisation"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-GB">http://www.cd-jackson.com/index.php/openhab/habmin/10-habmin-zwave-binding-initialisation</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-GB"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150945"><span lang="EN-GB">Creating items form things</span></a></h2>

<h3><a name="_Toc485150946"><span lang="EN-GB">The concept of </span></a><span lang="EN-US">Things, Channels, Items and Links</span></h3>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-GB">Before we start please read first the
concept of </span><span lang="EN-US">Things, Channels, Items and Links which is
directly tanken from the openHAB2 User Manual page </span><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/concepts/index.html#things-channels-items-and-links"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">http://docs.openhab.org/concepts/index.html#things-channels-items-and-links</span></span></a><span lang="EN-US"> </span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Things are the entities that can be
physically added to a system and which can potentially provide many
functionalities at once. It is important to note that things do not have to be
devices, but they can also represent a web service or any other manageable
source of information and functionality. Things provide their functionality
through a set of Channels. Channels are “passive” and can be regarded as a
declaration of a Thing, what it can offer. It is up to the individual setup,
which of the Channels are actively used through Items (see below).</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Items represent (fine-grained)
functionality that is used by applications - as user interfaces or automation
logic. Items have a state and they can receive commands.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The glue between Things and Items are
Links. Links are associations between exactly one Thing Channel and one Item.
If a Channel is linked to an Item, it is “enabled”, which means that the
functionality that the Item represents is handled through the given Channel.
Channels can be linked to multiple Items and Items can be linked to multiple
Channels.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">To illustrate these concepts, take a
two-channel actuator that controls two lights:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><img id="Picture 98" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image147.png" alt="http://docs.openhab.org/concepts/images/thing-devices-1.png" border="0" height="357" width="589"></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The actuator is the Thing. This might be
installed in the electrical cabinet, it has a physical address and needs to be
setup and configured in order to be used. The user is instead interested in the
two lights, which are located at different locations in his home. These lights
are the desired functionality, thus the Items and they are linked to the
Channels of the actuator. A Link can be regarded like a physical wire in this
example.</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The basic process of in PAPER UI is
explained on: </span><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/tutorials/beginner/configuration.html"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">http://docs.openhab.org/tutorials/beginner/configuration.html</span></span></a><span lang="EN-US"> </span></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc485150947"><span lang="EN-US">Creating the required items for my
project</span></a></h3>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">-Configuration</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">--Things </span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">and select the KeyFob_Gen5 thing</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span style="position: absolute; z-index: 251687936; margin-left: 19px; margin-top: 95px; width: 18px; height: 19px;"><img src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image152.jpg" height="19" width="18"></span><img id="Picture 148" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image153.jpg" border="0" height="142" width="283"></p>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><b><img id="Picture 159" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image154.jpg" border="0" height="90" width="151"></b></p>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">The next window will allow you to configure the item
  you want to link to the thing channel</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">You can also change the name of the item if you are
  planning to run with your own naming convention</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Then select &lt;LINK&gt; to create your new item</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 160" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image155.jpg" border="0" height="113" width="210"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Now the blue icon to the left of the name will
  change (white dot in the center)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">By clicking on this icon the channel will expand and
  show you the linked items to this cannel</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 161" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image156.jpg" border="0" height="87" width="265"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">You can now find the new item in</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">-Configuration</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">--Items </span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 244.45pt;" valign="top" width="326">

  </td>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span style="color: rgb(91, 155, 213);">DUMMYITEM_SamsungTV_Power</span></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</tbody></table>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150949"><span lang="EN-US">Chapter 11: Creating a dashboard
for your home automation project</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Every User Interface on openHAB2 is
providing its own style of dashboards to control your home automation project,
display current item states and attribute values or even include online
information like web pages.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">In our configuration of openHAB2 you will
have the choice of 4 different user interfaces which can be selected </span></p>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 239.3pt;" valign="top" width="319">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Start openHAB2 start screen </span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Direct URL: </span><span lang="EN-US">http://xxx.xxx.xxx.xxx:8080/
  start/index</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Here you will now find the GUIs:</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&lt;BASIC UI&gt;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">(requires setup using textual *.sitemap files)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&lt;PAPER UI&gt;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">(which were already using to configure openHAB2)</span></p>

  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">(this UI is all about creating a dashboard)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&lt;HABMIN&gt;</span></p>

  devices)</span></p>
  </td>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150950"><span lang="EN-US">BASIC UI dashboard</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Since this is a beginner’s tutorial where I
am trying to get things done using as less textual coding as possible, I will
not go into the details of creating a dashboard for the BASIC UI since it
requires the file based approach. </span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Tough you might find that some specific
requirements to a dashboard can only be solved creating this textual sitemap
configuration and using BASIC UI for displaying your dashboard.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">You can find more information in how to
setup and use BASIC UI on:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/configuration/sitemaps.html"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">http://docs.openhab.org/configuration/sitemaps.html</span></span></a></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><b><span style="font-size: 13pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri Light&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></b></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150951"><span lang="EN-US">PAPER UI dashboard</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The simplest way of creating an interactive
user interface is in just clicking on the &lt;CONTROL&gt; tab to PAPTER UI. Now
you should see all the items grouped by the things they belong to.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">You can also easily create different tabs
of things by adding &lt;Location&gt; information to the thing in the thing tab:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">NOTE: I had issues in updating a few
things, so it will be good to it while creating the things</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><img id="Picture 168" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image161.jpg" border="0" height="272" width="570"></p>

various tabs with items grouped by their things</span></p>

<h2><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></h2>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150953"><span lang="EN-US">HABMIN dashboard</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">And once again, since this is a beginner’s
tutorial I can’t go into all the possibilities of how to create a dashboard in
openHAB2. So I will not go into creating a dashboard in HABMIN. But be aware
the HABMIN is providing a powerful graphical way of creating dashboards you
might want to have a look at.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">You can find the standard documentation on:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/addons/uis/habmin/readme.html"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">http://docs.openhab.org/addons/uis/habmin/readme.html</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h1><a name="_Toc485150954"><span lang="EN-US">Chapter 12: Creating rules</span></a></h1>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Since rules can’t be configured using the
PAPER UI (stable version) you now have to go to the text files for now. For this
part we will now use the </span><span lang="EN-GB">Eclipse Smart Home Designer
since it creates at least some syntax highlighting.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">REMARK: You might find already some
functionality about configuration of rules in the PAPER UI snapshot versions so
there will be some changes in the way of doing rules more easily in the future.
Also HABmin is providing some kind of graphical rule engine.</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150955"><span lang="EN-GB">Creating the myfirstrule.rules
file</span></a></h2>

<table class="MsoTableGrid" style="border: medium none ; border-collapse: collapse;" border="1" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
 <tbody><tr>
  <td style="border: 1pt solid windowtext; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Start </span><span lang="EN-GB">Eclipse Smart Home
  Designer on your PC</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">Make sure you have mapped the Raspbian samba drive
  to your PC and </span><span lang="EN-US">Start </span><span lang="EN-GB">Eclipse
  Smart Home Designer is set to the right folder in this samba drive (see Chapter
  7: Installation of Eclipse Smart Home Designer -: part launching first time)</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">You should now the augmented icons for the different
  folders</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB">If you check the Rules folder you will only find a
  readme.txt file</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: solid solid solid none; border-color: windowtext windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: 1pt 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 180" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image167.jpg" border="0" height="279" width="274"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">You need to create a file with the ending .rules to
  store your rules there.</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">The fastest way of doing it is using the basic file
  management functionality of </span><span lang="EN-GB">Eclipse Smart Home
  Designer</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Right click on the readme.txt file and select copy</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 181" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image168.jpg" border="0" height="280" width="267"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Then right click again and select Paste</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 183" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image169.jpg" border="0" height="279" width="267"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">A new window will ask you to enter a new file name.</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 182" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image170.jpg" border="0" height="98" width="250"></p>
  </td>
 </tr>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Change the file name to</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">myfirstrule.rules</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">an press </span>&lt;OK&gt;</p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 184" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image171.jpg" border="0" height="99" width="251"></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">myfirstrule.rules</p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;OK&gt;</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">A new file will appear in the Rules folder showing
  the rule icon</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">

  </td>

  <td style="border-style: none solid solid; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 173.45pt;" valign="top" width="231">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">Now double click on the file to open it and delete
  the old content to have a plain rule rile</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span lang="EN-US">And save the rule file again</span></p>
  </td>
  <td style="border-style: none solid solid none; border-color: -moz-use-text-color windowtext windowtext -moz-use-text-color; border-width: medium 1pt 1pt medium; padding: 0cm 5.4pt; width: 319.25pt;" valign="top" width="426">
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;"><img id="Picture 187" src="openHAB2_Raspberry_beginner-s_walkthrough_files/image173.jpg" border="0" height="52" width="396"></p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;ctrl+a&gt;</p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;del&gt;</p>
  <p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 0.0001pt; line-height: normal;">&lt;ctrlss&gt;</p>
  </td>
 </tr>
</tbody></table>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<h2><a name="_Toc485150956"><span lang="EN-US">Creating a basic rules</span></a></h2>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">I will try to give some basic rule examples
to start with but you have to be aware:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><b><span style="color: red;" lang="EN-US">DISCLAIMER:</span></b></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><b><i><span style="color: red;" lang="EN-US">I am no coding
expert at all and writing rules is still the most difficult part in my home
automation project (finding the right commands, the right syntax and so on), so
you might be better off using to other tutorials</span></i></b><i><span style="color: red;" lang="EN-US">.</span></i></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">For the standard rules documentation incl.
the rule syntax please refer to the online documentation:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="http://docs.openhab.org/configuration/rules-dsl.html"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">http://docs.openhab.org/configuration/rules-dsl.html</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">You can also find some rules samples on:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><a href="https://github.com/openhab/openhab1-addons/wiki/Samples-Rules"><span class="Heading9Char"><span style="font-size: 10pt; line-height: 115%; color: windowtext; text-decoration: none;" lang="EN-US">https://github.com/openhab/openhab1-addons/wiki/Samples-Rules</span></span></a></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">And maybe some coding experts in the
community will find the time to create a kind of an openHAB2 compendium to make
it easier the non-experts to do rules.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">REMAKR: Yes, I know there are plenty of
online documentation sites available, but the problem for me was the “plenty”
part of it since I always had to go through plenty different websites to finally
get the syntax right and make the rule do, what I wanted it to do.</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></p>

<span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 115%; font-family: &quot;Calibri&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US"><br style="page-break-before: always;" clear="all">
</span>

<p class="MsoNormal"><b><span style="font-family: &quot;Calibri Light&quot;,&quot;sans-serif&quot;;" lang="EN-US">&nbsp;</span></b></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc485150957"><span lang="EN-US">Basic rule example:</span></a></h3>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">We will use the:</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">KeyFob_Gen5</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">to control some items linked to</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Z-Wave Node 2: FGS223 Double Switch 2</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Z-Wave Node 3: MSP-3-1-X1 Z-Wave Plus Micro
Smart Plug ON/OFF</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Yamaha Receiver RX-V581</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">DUMMYTHING_SamsungTV</span></p>

<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">HF-LPB100-ZJ200 (WiFi LED)</span></p>
